According to one film scholar, the song and the entire theater scene marks the disintegration of Betty's and Rita's personalities, as well as their relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nochimson_35-6"><a href="#cite_note-nochimson-35">[35]</a></sup> With the use of multiple languages and a song to portray such primal emotions, one film analyst states that Lynch exhibits his distrust of intellectual discourse and chooses to make sense through images and sounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hudson_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-hudson-23">[23]</a></sup> The disorienting effect of the music playing although del Rio is no longer there is described as "the musical version of <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Magritte" title="RenÃ© Magritte">Magritte</a>'s painting <i><a href="/wiki/The_Treachery_of_Images" title="The Treachery of Images">Ceci n'est pas une pipe</a></i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOdellLe_Blanc2007162_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOdellLe_Blanc2007162-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mulholland_Drive_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mulholland_drive(lynch)--.jpg"><img alt="Four people stand beside each other facing off-camera, from left to right: a blonde woman wearing a tan dress suit, a man with salt-and-pepper hair wearing a blazer over white shirt and slacks, a brunette wearing red pants and a black top, and a dark-haired man wearing a black leather jacket over black clothes." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="397" data-file-width="596" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mulholland_drive%28lynch%29--.jpg/250px-Mulholland_drive%28lynch%29--.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mulholland_drive%28lynch%29--.jpg/375px-Mulholland_drive%28lynch%29--.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mulholland_drive%28lynch%29--.jpg/500px-Mulholland_drive%28lynch%29--.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mulholland_drive(lynch)--.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Naomi Watts, David Lynch, Laura Elena Harring and Justin Theroux at the <a href="/wiki/2001_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2001 Cannes Film Festival">2001 Cannes Film Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Mulholland Drive</i> premiered at the <a href="/wiki/2001_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2001 Cannes Film Festival">2001 Cannes Film Festival</a> in May to major critical acclaim. Lynch was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Best_Director_Award_(Cannes_Film_Festival)" title="Best Director Award (Cannes Film Festival)">Best Director prize</a> at the festival, sharing it with co-winner <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joel_Coen" title="Joel Coen">Joel Coen</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Wasn%27t_There_(2001_film)" title="The Man Who Wasn't There (2001 film)">The Man Who Wasn't There</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cannes_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-cannes-84">[84]</a></sup> It drew positive reviews from many critics and some of the strongest audience reactions of Lynch's career.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mulholland_Drive_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">Universal Pictures</a> released <i>Mulholland Drive</i> theatrically in 66 theaters in the United States on October 12, 2001, grossing $587,591 over its opening weekend. It eventually expanded to its widest release of 247 theaters, ultimately grossing $7,220,243 at the U.S. box office. <a href="/wiki/TVA_Films" title="TVA Films">TVA Films</a> released the film theatrically in Canada on October 26, 2001. In other territories outside the United States, the film grossed $12,892,096 for a worldwide total of $20,112,339.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mulholland_Drive_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since its release, <i>Mulholland Drive</i> has, according to film scholars Jay R. Letzner and Donald R. Ross, "garnered both some of the harshest epithets and some of the most lavish praise in recent cinematic history".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> It received acclaim from many critics; even <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i>, who had given negative or mixed reviews to most of Lynch's previous films, awarded the film four stars and commented, "David Lynch has been working toward <i>Mulholland Drive</i> all of his career, and now that he's arrived there I forgive him for <i><a href="/wiki/Wild_at_Heart_(film)" title="Wild at Heart (film)">Wild at Heart</a></i> (1990) and even <i><a href="/wiki/Lost_Highway_(film)" title="Lost Highway (film)">Lost Highway</a></i> (1997). At last his experiment doesn't shatter the test tubes. The movie is a surrealist dreamscape in the form of a Hollywood <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">film noir</a>, and the less sense it makes, the more we can't stop watching it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebert_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-ebert-49">[49]</a></sup> Ebert subsequently added <i>Mulholland Drive</i> to his "Great Films" list in November 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, Stephen Holden said that the film "ranks alongside <a href="/wiki/Federico_Fellini" title="Federico Fellini">Fellini</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/8%C2%BD" title="8Â½">8Â½</a></i> and other <a href="/wiki/Auteur" title="Auteur">auteurist</a> fantasias as a monumental self-reflection" and added, "Looked at lightly, it is the grandest and silliest cinematic carnival to come along in quite some time: a lurching journey through one filmmaker's personal fun house. On a more serious level, its investigation into the power of movies pierces a void from which you can hear the screams of a ravenous demon whose appetites can never be slaked."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-holden_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-holden-30">[30]</a></sup> Edward Guthmann of the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> called it "exhilaratingÂ ... for its dreamlike images and fierce, frequently reckless imagination" and added, "there's a mesmerizing quality to its languid pace, its sense of foreboding and its lost-in-time atmosphereÂ ... it holds us, spellbound and amused, for all of its loony and luscious, exasperating 146Â minutes [and] proves that Lynch is in solid formâand still an expert at pricking our nerves."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a> observed, "<i>Mulholland Drive</i> makes movies feel alive again. This sinful pleasure is a fresh triumph for Lynch, and one of the best films of a sorry-ass year. For visionary daring, swooning eroticism and colors that pop like a whore's lip gloss, there's nothing like this baby anywhere."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> J. Hoberman of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i> stated, "This voluptuous phantasmagoriaÂ ... is certainly Lynch's strongest movie since <i>Blue Velvet</i> and maybe <i><a href="/wiki/Eraserhead" title="Eraserhead">Eraserhead</a></i>. The very things that failed him in the bad-boy rockabilly debacle of <i>Lost Highway</i>âthe atmosphere of free-floating menace, pointless transmigration of souls, provocatively dropped plot stitches, gimcrack alternate universesâare here brilliantly rehabilitated."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hoberman_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-hoberman-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>While reviews of the film were mostly positive (receiving an 82% rating on film <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> <i>Mulholland Drive</i> was not without its detractors. <a href="/wiki/Rex_Reed" title="Rex Reed">Rex Reed</a> of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_New_York_Observer" title="The New York Observer">The New York Observer</a></i> said that it was the worst film he had seen in 2001, calling it "a load of moronic and incoherent garbage."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i>, Peter Rainer observed, "Although I like it more than some of his other dreamtime freakfests, it's still a pretty moribund rideÂ ... Lynch needs to renew himself with an influx of the deep feeling he has for people, for outcasts, and lay off the cretins and hobgoblins and zombies for a while."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, Desson Howe called it "an extended mood opera, if you want to put an arty label on incoherence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Todd_McCarthy" title="Todd McCarthy">Todd McCarthy</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> found much to praiseâ"Lynch cranks up the levels of bizarre humor, dramatic incident and genuine mystery with a succession of memorable scenes, some of which rank with his best"âbut also noted, "the film jumps off the solid ground of relative narrative coherence into Lynchian fantasylandÂ ... for the final 45Â minutes, Lynch is in mind-twisting mode that presents a form of alternate reality with no apparent meaning or logical connection to what came before. Although such tactics are familiar from <i>Twin Peaks</i> and elsewhere, the sudden switcheroo to head games is disappointing because, up to this point, Lynch had so wonderfully succeeded in creating genuine involvement."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mccarthy_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-mccarthy-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Berardinelli" title="James Berardinelli">James Berardinelli</a> also criticized it, saying: "Lynch cheats his audience, pulling the rug out from under us. He throws everything into the mix with the lone goal of confusing us. Nothing makes any sense because it's not supposed to make any sense. There's no purpose or logic to events. Lynch is playing a big practical joke on us."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Film theorist <a href="/wiki/Ray_Carney" title="Ray Carney">Ray Carney</a> notes, "You wouldn't need all the emotional back-flips and narrative trap doors if you had anything to say. You wouldn't need doppelgangers and shadow-figures if your characters had souls."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later, <i>Mulholland Drive</i> was named the best film of the decade by the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Film_Critics_Association" title="Los Angeles Film Critics Association">Los Angeles Film Critics Association</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Cahiers_du_cin%C3%A9ma" title="Cahiers du cinÃ©ma">Cahiers du cinÃ©ma</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IndieWire" title="IndieWire">IndieWire</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> <i>Reverse Shot</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Time_Out_(magazine)" title="Time Out (magazine)">Time Out New York</a></i>, who asked rhetorically in a reference to the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, "Can there be another movie that speaks as resonantlyÂ â if unwittinglyÂ â to the awful moment that marked our decade?Â ... <i>Mulholland Drive</i> is the monster behind the diner; it's the self-delusional dream turned into nightmare."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> It was also voted best of the decade in a <i><a href="/wiki/Film_Comment" title="Film Comment">Film Comment</a></i> poll of international "critics, programmers, academics, filmmakers and others",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and by the magazine's readers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> It appeared on lists among the ten best films of the decade, coming in third according to <i>The Guardian</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i> critic Peter Travers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> the Canadian Press,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Access_Hollywood" title="Access Hollywood">Access Hollywood</a></i> critic Scott Mantz,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and eighth on critic <a href="/wiki/Michael_Phillips_(critic)" title="Michael Phillips (critic)">Michael Phillips</a>' list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> In 2010 it was named the second best <a href="/wiki/Art_film" title="Art film">arthouse film</a> ever by <i>The Guardian</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The film was voted as the 11th best film set in Los Angeles in the last 25 years by a group of <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> writers and editors with the primary criterion of communicating an inherent truth about the L.A. experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine placed <i>Mulholland Drive</i> at number 391 on their list of the five hundred greatest films ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> It has also been ranked number 38 on the <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> program <i><a href="/wiki/50_Films_to_See_Before_You_Die" title="50 Films to See Before You Die">50 Films to See Before You Die</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> In 2011, online magazine <a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a> named <i>Mulholland Drive</i> in its piece on "New Classics" as the most enduring film since 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/British_Film_Institute" title="British Film Institute">British Film Institute</a>'s 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/Sight_%26_Sound" title="Sight &amp; Sound">Sight &amp; Sound</a></i> poll, <i>Mulholland Drive</i> was ranked the 28th greatest film ever made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Having received 40 critics' votes, it is one of only two films from the 21st century to be included in the list, along with 2000's <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Mood_for_Love" title="In the Mood for Love">In the Mood for Love</a></i>. In a 2015 <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> poll, it was ranked 21st among all American films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The following year, <i>Mulholland Drive</i> was named as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/100_Greatest_Films_of_the_21st_Century" title="100 Greatest Films of the 21st Century">greatest film of the 21st century</a> in a poll conducted by <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC Culture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mulholland_Drive_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> was released in April 2002 in the United States and Canada, with few special features. It was released without chapter stops, a feature that Lynch objects to on the grounds that it "demystifies" the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> In spite of Lynch's concerns, the DVD release included a cover insert that provided "David Lynch's 10 Clues to Unlocking This Thriller", although one DVD reviewer noted that the clues may be "big obnoxious <a href="/wiki/Red_herring" title="Red herring">red herrings</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-horan_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-horan-72">[72]</a></sup> Nick Coccellato of Eccentric Cinema gave the film a rating of nine out of ten and the DVD release an eight out of ten, saying that the lack of special features "only adds to the mystery the film itself possesses, in abundance."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-EC-119">[119]</a></sup> Special features in later versions and overseas versions of the DVD include a Lynch interview at the Cannes Film Festival and highlights of the debut of the film at Cannes.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Optimum_Releasing" title="Optimum Releasing">Optimum Home Entertainment</a> released <i>Mulholland Drive</i> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc#Region_codes" title="Blu-ray Disc">European market</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray</a> as part of its StudioCanal Collection on September 13, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> New special features exclusive to this release include: an introduction by Thierry Jousse; <i>In the Blue Box</i>, a retrospective documentary featuring directors and critics; two making-of documentaries: <i>On the Road to Mulholland Drive</i> and <i>Back to Mulholland Drive</i>, and several interviews with people involved in making the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> It is the second David Lynch film in this line of Blu-rays after <a href="/wiki/The_Elephant_Man_(film)" title="The Elephant Man (film)"><i>The Elephant Man</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 15, 2015, <a href="/wiki/The_Criterion_Collection" title="The Criterion Collection">The Criterion Collection</a> announced that it would release <i>Mulholland Drive</i>, newly restored through a <a href="/wiki/4K_resolution" title="4K resolution">4K</a> digital transfer, on DVD and Blu-ray on October 27, 2015, both of which include new interviews with the film's crew and the 2005 edition of Chris Rodley's book <i><a href="/wiki/Lynch_on_Lynch" title="Lynch on Lynch">Lynch on Lynch</a></i>, along with the original trailer and other extras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-October_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-October-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> It was Lynch's second film to receive a Criterion Collection release on DVD and Blu-ray, proceeding <i>Eraserhead</i> which was released in September 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mulholland_Drive_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lynch was nominated for an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Best Director</a> for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oscars_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-oscars-126">[126]</a></sup> From the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hollywood_Foreign_Press" title="Hollywood Foreign Press">Hollywood Foreign Press</a>, the film received four <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe</a> nominations, including Best Picture (Drama), Best Director and Best Screenplay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldenglobes_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-goldenglobes-127">[127]</a></sup> It was named Best Picture by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Film_Critics_Circle_Awards" title="New York Film Critics Circle Awards">New York Film Critics Circle</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2001_New_York_Film_Critics_Circle_Awards" title="2001 New York Film Critics Circle Awards">2001 New York Film Critics Circle Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Online_Film_Critics_Society_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Online Film Critics Society Award for Best Picture">Online Film Critics Society</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mulholland_Drive_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">

And it's essential to hold that world together, to keep it safe."
